#  [](/thread/172963-tonys-two-candle-trading-system)Tony's Two Candle trading system 

  * 

  * [#1](/thread/172963-tonys-two-candle-trading-system "Post Permalink")

  * First Post: Edited Jun 5, 2009 1:38pm  Jun 3, 2009 1:32pm | Edited Jun 5, 2009 1:38pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar55255_6.gif) tony_dtrader](tony_dtrader)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Аdministrator | [310 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=55255)

Howdy Folks,  
  
Just wanted to share a high probability trading system to you. Its very simple, just pull out a 1hour chart any currency.  
  
Now simply wait for a bull or bear candle to form, after it closes bullish or bearish, ITS MOST LIKELY the next candle will form bull or bear candle...theres some easy pips for you.  
  
Examples:   
  
Bull candle at 8gmt, most likely 9gmt candle could be a bull candle too.  
Bear candle at 11gmt, most likely 12gmt candle could be a bear too.  
  
Entry Exit Rules:  
Bull candle --- Stoploss at the low of the previous candle, target 10-20pips or the close of the next candle.  
Bear candle --- Stoploss at the high of the previous candle, target 10-20pips or the close of the next candle.  
No trade --- If next candle starts to form against the direction of the previous candle.  
  
Note: The best bull or bear candles are ones that are one-sided or ones that have little or no wick. (strong bull/bear candle)  
  
More info, template and filters on this post --- [http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=112](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=2781325&postcount=112)  
Happy Pippin ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)

Its just a simple trading system and it matters not if its a ranging market or a trending one, because we aren't riding trends, we're just dealing with 2 candles to make some easy gains.   
  
Simply wait for a bull candle and see if the next candle forms bullish, by say 5pips and you can enter for a 10-20pip target, stoploss at the low of the previous one.  
  
If the candle is bull and the next one isn;t forming bullish, its a no trade. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
Best times to trade are from european open to new york close 

prepare for worst & expect the best

yes i trade this live on 50lots, mostly only trading this on usdjpy since it has a less volatility and stoploss/spread than other pair.  
  
I only recommend using this on 1hour chart and trading only from european to new york session, because we need a market that moves to profit and not a sleepy market with small candles.  
  
In my broker fxdd, from 9:00 to 24:00 , thats 15 hours and 15 candles per day to trade.  
  
This system is just pure price action, if buyers pushed the price up in the past hour, its more likely buyers will push the price up again on the next hour, vice versa for sellers. 

prepare for worst & expect the best

hi,  
that is a very simply system. i notice that the candle before 1st candle is always the opposite direction.   
i.e.   
0th candle - bear candle  
1st candle - bull candle  
2nd candle- bull (5 pips) and then buy  
close at the end of 2nd candle or 10/20 pips  
stop loss 0th candle low  
  
any one can make a EA to test it out?  
  
  
happy trading

i think the condition for the trade is.   
  
Previous candle bull candle, current candle move +5 pips u buy with TP 10/20 SL previous candle low  
  
Previous candle bear candle, current candle move -5 pips u sell with TP 10/20 SL previous candle high

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar55255_6.gif) tony_dtrader](tony_dtrader)

> [Quoting forexisfx](/thread/post/2774569#post2774569 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> i think this thread will end when somebody make an EA and discover that the equity goes down hill in a run long. So no EA please. At least let this thread stay alive for 24 hours. I might be wrong , let see how this goes.
> 
> Ignored

Dude i understand your skepticism,  
  
Let me tell you something. Tell me whats better?  
  
1\. a dozen of lagging and lieing indicators and a system that keeps you exposed into the market (more exposure more risk) to make a 100 pips on speculation of prices.  
  
or  
  
2\. A system thats just price action and that can give u a 80-90% chance of earning 10-20 pips in just an hour or less of exposure into the market.  
  
\----  
  
If you browse through the hourly chart and you will notice 8/10 times after a bull candle forms the next candle forms into a bull and vice versa for a bear candles. If you see a bull candle, u see the next candle forming into a bull right in front of your eyes and you also see its gone 5pips from the close of the first candle.... Thats like the highest bet you can take for making some kind of immediate gain from the market, like 10-20 easy pips.  
  
I bet you that everyone will agree that theres no mechanical system on earth that can profit in the longrun with low risks, simply because the market doesn't move mechanically.  
  
Theres no way to know which way the price will head next.. it could go up it could go down.  
  
I just use this strategy to make my 20-40 pips daily, If you use about 10% of your account and bank on 20-40pips daily, thats a 2-4% daily gain and in 20 trading days a month thats a 40-80% easy gains, isn't it?  
  
When you speak of EA, its like your trying to make all the pips of the market and a automated system that will over trade the market mechanically on your behalf.  
  
It doesn't work that way, because 50% is the traders system and 50% is the traders instincts and his plans of what he wants from the market, that will eventually decide what is profitable in the long term. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

prepare for worst & expect the best

Hi, The stoploss is just for protection purposes, in event the market suddenly turns a 100 pip against you, you could exit off with a limited loss.  
  
Ideally you should exit if the price moves 5-10 pips against you and accept the tiny loss instead of a big one. There are many more opportunities that will arrive again, so you can try again.  
  
The old saying, cut off the losers and let run the winners.   
  
Remember its a 2 candle strategy and not a 3-4-6-8 candle strategy, but if you feel it could trend more, its best to break even the trade to allow it to run for more. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

prepare for worst & expect the best

Hey i have something to help you guys with price action on the minutely scale, just to keep you alert about whats happening inside the 1hour candle.  
  
copy .mq4 to experts/indicators folder  
extract and copy .tpl to templates folder  
restart metatrader and load the template "twocandlesystem_m1monitor"  
Load it on a 1minute chart.  
Should look like the image attached.

  * Jun 3, 2009 5:50pm  Jun 3, 2009 5:50pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar55255_6.gif) tony_dtrader](tony_dtrader)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Аdministrator | [310 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=55255)

> [Quoting ronrhodes](/thread/post/2774977#post2774977 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Tony, thanks.  
>    
>  Does the price action often (what percentage of the time?) go back against the first candle quite a bit during the hour (quite a bit, even most of the hour?)...and then come back in the first candle's direction later in the hour, and then close in the happy direction?  
>    
>  Would you discuss this just a bit, to give us a sense of the "guts" it may sometimes take to stay in the trade?  
>    
>  Ron
> 
> Ignored

Lets take an example.  
  
candle 1 is a bear, candle 2 is a bull... so we wait to see if candle 3 forms into a bull by 5pips. Then we enter the trade and it should start moving rightaway, if it doesn't and starts to move 5-10 pips against you, thats a alert that you may need to exit the trade since its not moving that well.  
  
Vice versa for bear, candle 0 must be a bull, candle 1 must be a bear and we wait for candle 3 to form into a bearish by 5pips to enter.  
  
Remember i trade usdjpy, which has a daily range of about 80-100 pips on average. so 10 pips is quite a lot on that pair and it usually takes 30-40 mins to move 10-20 pips, unlike gbpusd or eurusd that does 30-50pip in a average hour candle.  
  
Please consider my system and high probability bet to make some quick pips, its not that i havent lost bets, but from experience i make sure strictly that my losers are less and small and make sure the winners are more and big.  
  
As ive said before the best bear and bull candles are ones that have little to no wicks before turning bearish of bullish, that indicates a strong buying or selling.  
  
hope this helps 

prepare for worst & expect the best

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar71675_5.gif) Alberto_Jazz](alberto_jazz)

  * Joined Jun 2008 | Status: Trader | [593 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=71675)

I think we have to work whit this trade off:  
  
1\. Trade with high % winning trades but a bad rawal (average win / average loss) placing large stop losses  
2\. Trade with low % winning trades but good rawal placing small stop losses.  
  
A solution could be to settle the stop and then calculate the target profit as: stop loss*Ratio (for instance 1.5).   
In this way I will obtain a system with a good rawal and a stop that is not to small.

I have just read the thread twice (short threads are great to get the gist of) and I have to say that the simplicity of this system could make it successful  
  
Far to many of you are asking questions that have been answered. In comparison to alot of threads that involve rediculous indicators and rules to trade, this could be read, understood and traded by a teenager.  
  
Re read the thread until you a perfectly clear on how it works Then try it for a while. It is a simple hour by hour trade that requires nothing more than a candle followed by another candle. If it is in the right direction trade, if not dont trade, if your not comfortable with it, get a cup of coffee, put your feet up and relax.  
  
Far to many of you want answers before your prepared to look for them. The answers are on the first few pages.  
  
Nice work BTW

> [Quoting Alberto_Jazz](/thread/post/2775558#post2775558 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I agree. The stop is too tight to obtain 80% winning ratio.
> 
> Ignored

Whilst the SL is a little tight, it does also allow a trader to get better R/R returns. Im not going to pretend I trade this method, I just like it for its simplicity, however I trade IBs. Some of the best IBs (Inside Bars) have had a pip range of 8-16 pips. Sure there are times you get stopped out, thats part of trading, however the chances to run 1:1 are greater giving you choices to take partial profits and allow trades to run. Whether traders adopt some of there own thinking to these simple methods is up to them. So in that case if your SL is tight, sure 80% may be a bit rich, you wont know till youve tried it, but how you manage your trade is the key.   
  
Win rate is only relative in situations where traders only take 1:1 or 1:2 R/R, if traders have patience and do string some 1:5s or better, then a lower Win rate can still equate to Positive growth.

  * Jun 4, 2009 1:15am  Jun 4, 2009 1:15am 

  * [ mikkom](mikkom)

  * Joined Mar 2008 | Status: Still testing and trading | [1,453 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=63087)

> [Quoting tony_dtrader](/thread/post/2774980#post2774980 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I trade only the usdjpy mostly with this, sometimes eurjpy. Haven't tried it on other pairs since their too volatile and would move 20-30 pip against me many times, which is too risky for me.
> 
> Ignored

Here is USDJPY with **very** simple rules and h1 (please confirm if I understood the first post correctly) I don't have long m1 data for usdjpy so this is not as reliable as it should be.  
  
Bull candle: previous candle must be a "good" bull candle, open is at lower 25% of the candle and close is at upper 25% of the candle. Vice versa for bear candles.  
  
I enter at new bar open + (- for shorts) 10 pips (with buy/sell stop) and target 20 pips (with tp). Stop loss is always at previous candle low.  
  
Note that I don't use any indicators here, just the rules from the first post.  
  
H1 Curve below: 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: TesterGraph.gif
Size: 8 KB](/attachment/image/255153/thumbnail?d=1365572749)](/attachment/image/255153?d=1244045584)

For me the rules were  
for long:  
-down candle  
-then up candle (without 25% rule)  
-next candle we enter if it goes up too  
  
so we try to trade swings

>  -down candle

>  -next candle we enter if it goes up too

The point of 25% rule was to target the "best" bull candles to see if there is potential in the "best" setups of this system.  
  
Here are the results for the above rules (down candle, up candle, stop at +-5 from open and 20 pips tp)  
  
If a tp is not hit during the candle, position is closed at the next candle open.

  * | Joined Aug 2007  | Status: Trader | [889 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=45947)

> [Quoting Razor_trader](/thread/post/2775620#post2775620 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I have just read the thread twice (short threads are great to get the gist of) and I have to say that the simplicity of this system could make it successful  
>    
>  Far to many of you are asking questions that have been answered. In comparison to alot of threads that involve rediculous indicators and rules to trade, this could be read, understood and traded by a teenager.  
>    
>  Re read the thread until you a perfectly clear on how it works Then try it for a while. It is a simple hour by hour trade that requires nothing more than a candle followed by another...
> 
> Ignored

  
Razor you have to understand simple doesn't necessarily mean long term profitable. Sure its simple and its very large hearted of Tony to post it and yes I assume he's been profitable with it thats why he's posting it but for how long has he been trading it? To even consider trading a system its very important to back test to see how its done in the past more importantly the immediate past. How do you know its not a lucky streak?   
  
I agree that far too many people want answers before they are prepared to look for them but unfortunately none of the answers we want are on the first few pages as the method hasn't been traded long term by tony.  
  
I'm just trying to say simple doesn't necessarily mean long term profitable.   
It has to be tested and even though I know its subjective. How can you say "simplicity of this sytem could make it successful" as far as I know there's no relationship between simplicity and success in the trading world. Complicated systems like fuzzy logic and neuroshell systems can be just as successful as simple breakout ones.

  * Jun 4, 2009 3:38am  Jun 4, 2009 3:38am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar55255_6.gif) tony_dtrader](tony_dtrader)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Аdministrator | [310 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=55255)

> [Quoting pipchaser1](/thread/post/2776771#post2776771 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> tony......  
>  do you need to wait for another opposite candle after you tp on second candle or just use second candle as first candle on next set up? hope i explain that ok....  
>  thanks
> 
> Ignored

Its just common sense myfriend, if buyers or sellers pushed a candle and the next candle starts to form bearish or bullish due to the previous buy/sell pressure, so you take a trade to make some instant 10-20pip gain.  
  
After that you need to either break even if you haven't taken profit due to a chance that a 3rd candle will go in your direction or wait for an opposite candle and a new setup from there. 

prepare for worst & expect the best

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#84](/thread/post/2777391#post2777391 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 4, 2009 9:11am  Jun 4, 2009 9:11am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96744_2.gif) Razor_trader](razor_trader)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Getting closer to ...... | [1,787 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96744)

> [Quoting fugly](/thread/post/2776626#post2776626 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Razor you have to understand simple doesn't necessarily mean long term profitable. Sure its simple and its very large hearted of Tony to post it and yes I assume he's been profitable with it thats why he's posting it but for how long has he been trading it? To even consider trading a system its very important to back test to see how its done in the past more importantly the immediate past. How do you know its not a lucky streak?   
>    
>  I agree that far too many people want answers before they are prepared to look for them but unfortunately none of the...
> 
> Ignored

Heres the thing. People want systems that have long term, utimate profitability and very little loss over long periods. NOTHING will guarentee that, NOTHING has a long term, 100% always positive profit. You could have a very very good year, or 2 or 3 but you can bet that you will also have some lean years.  
  
Traders fail because they cannot compute this, they never want to loose, only ever want to win. This is why when you look back on the 95% of people on this forum you can guarentee that there posts are all over the place asking the same questions. WHY? Because they are looking for the HG and the 100% win rate that doubles, triples accounts over a short period. It aint going to happen. The strategys, Methods, Systems that promise this fall down big time in the end. You have great solid returns, dont understand it ultimatly and watch your account go bye bye when multiple trades dont work.  
  
Simple systems have a great chance at working because people can follow them easily, therefore identify setups during backtesting and being able to implement with ease during the now trading. Whilst I understand backtesting it is not a sure thing for something in the future and too much emphasis is placed on the success of backtesting, or the failure. If people trialled it on a demo they would get to know first hand whether a setup like this is good for them.  
  
Simple is simple. If your a trader that would prefer Stocastics, RSI, 14 different Moving averages, Bollinger Bands, TL, S/R with Gann fans and FIBs then tie that in with rediculous rules to define when to trade and not, then hey knock yourself out. BIG players trade simpler, they dont have time to play games with lagging indicators. Some of the charts and setups I have read about are more difficult to comprehend than the Bible (no offense).   
  
You cannot talk of future profit without first knowing the future, regardless of the system, and if your afraid of long term profitability then this is not the arena for you. People who are this way need to get a full time job and that is it (I still work full time job but not because I dont understand how things work). IF your sole goal is to find something that has is going to work in all weather then your kidding yourself. Traders understand drawdown periods, traders also understand that chopping and changing when things dont work out will usually lead down that darker path. This is a random arena, and despite the know how and rules, alot of the time the market does its random thing.  
  
BTW this is a reply to an overall thread not to your personally. Your points are valid, I just thought I would add information that has been posted for Eons yet few people are prepared to acknowledge  
  
Razor

> Disliked
> 
> Hi, The stoploss is just for protection purposes, in event the market suddenly turns a 100 pip against you, you could exit off with a limited loss.  
>    
>  _**Ideally you should exit if the price moves 5-10 pips against you and accept the tiny loss instead of a big one**_. There are many more opportunities that will arrive again, so you can try again.  
>    
>  The old saying, cut off the losers and let run the winners.   
>    
>  Remember its a 2 candle strategy and not a 3-4-6-8 candle strategy, but if you feel it could trend more, its best to break even the trade...
> 
> Ignored

With TP of 20 and SL of 5-10, we have both 80% chance of winning and a 2:1 RR. Fantastic isn't it ? Nothing can beat that.

Hey whats up, i will be demoing this for a few days to see how it goes.  
Right now i am in a demo trade on UJ here are the details:  
  
UJ: Short | Lower entry target: 96.11 | SL: 96.21 | TP: 96.01 | Spread:3  
  
I will post a picture with the trade and future trades i do tomorrow.   
Lets see how it goes. Will update on status.  
  
Update:  
  
I am still in the signal. A new h1 bar has just opened.  
I went all the way to +6. The signal bar closed at -2 for me so i am now waiting to see what the next bar will do.  
  
2nd Update:  
Well its 12am here in new york(EST) and a new bar just poped up and i am at -5. I went all the way down to +5.   
Now the last bar was a little doji so i dunno what to do. Since my stop is only -10 i will let it ride to see what happends. 

Time is what keeps everything from happening "right now".

Hi  
  
Great...sick of all the lagging indicators .....I just added the attached candle recognition master indi....helps a bit with the decision making.  
  
Thanks to the creator of this thread.  
  
Re the indi: When you attach it to your MT4 chart each candle that represents some candlestick pattern will be marked with the symbol. A legend for the symbols is located in the top left corner of the chart and you can easily find out which patter is represented by the specific symbol. Now, all you have to do is to buy after the strong bullish patterns and sell on the strong bearish patterns.

Its not just that some people doubt it could work, its just that the mind cannot comprehend the simplicity of it and interpret possible results. Too many traders shun the simple methods (probably because they also believe if its too good to be true yadda yadda) and go with the complex, rack your brains, fill your charts methods that are posted everywhere.  
  
Im not a fan of stating the profitability of a method before the method gets off the ground. For some reason people see this and they need hard results without devoting anytime to trialling it themselves. There are plenty of threads on here that claim high returns and the same thing happens, traders cut it down with questions and criticism before even reading and trialling the method. In some cases it is a good thing (protecting noob traders from the destruction of following a thread that promises rediculous results) however it is still ultimatly up to the individual to pick and choose and today there are more demo platforms opening daily so you can give a method a good trial before deciding to put the money on the table.  
  
So far this thread is starting to develope with some people taking active involvement. Time the mother of all will tell how successful this method can be.  
  
Razor

  * [#112](/thread/post/2781325#post2781325 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 5, 2009 1:37pm  Jun 5, 2009 1:37pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar55255_6.gif) tony_dtrader](tony_dtrader)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Аdministrator | [310 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=55255)

Folks,  
  
My strong suggestion is to trade only after 7GMT and max around 20GMT.  
  
Enter the market with a certain goal in mind, like 20-40pips or whatever you need, then stop trading.  
  
Not trading in right sessions, over trading and not having a goal n plan is not good for the health of a trader.  
  
For newbie, just practice on a demo. trade with no more than 10% of your demo money, target 20-40pips per day, thats 2-4% gains per day and 40-80% profit per month.  
  
Just imagine if you had a 100,000$ account and you make 40-80% of that per month, thats a killing 40-80k per months!!   
  
I have researched a good filter to prevent taking trades on consolidating candles. Here is the filter -  
  
1, add a 5 period smoothed moving average following HIGH prices.  
2, add a 5 period smoothed moving average following LOW prices.  
  
If the candles are inside of the moving averages, you might not want to consider trading & if the candle breaks out of the moving averages you might consider wanting to trade the next candle.  
  
Additionally, you might want to also use a 1minute chart to monitor price action on the minutely scale to see how good the trade is and for alert if the trade is going against you.  
  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...5&postcount=45](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=2774835&postcount=45)  
  
Wish you all Happy pipping! Please find all the answers to your quessy's by reading through the posts.  
  
Cya laters,  
Tony

Whilst I am with you so far on the simplicity of the concept, best not to warp the imaginations of people by this post. Imagination and reality are 2 separate concepts, imagining things such as making 80K a month is not realistic unless you account allows it (it would have be much larger the 100K) If you were able to double a 100K account in a year that would be fantastic.   
  
And 10% of an account on any trade will lead to emotional killing when you string 3 or more loosers together. A more rational approach, at 100K at least would be 2.5-3%. Rome wasnt built in a day which is why so much of it still stand today. Trade safely and for the longevity of it, not risk more than you need to.

smurf, looking good! ... like you are finding your answers. But what does "different levels of learning" have to do with plain written posts there in black and white (again, no offense. Just to help 'get to it')?   
  
Tony, in post #9 as you already read:  
  
"...mostly only trading this on usdjpy since it has a less volatility and stoploss/spread than other pair.  
  
I only recommend using this on 1hour chart and trading only from european to [probably Tony should have said "through" NY session] new york session, because we need a market that moves to profit and not a sleepy market with small candles.  
  
In my broker fxdd, from 9:00 to 24:00 , thats 15 hours and 15 candles per day to trade.    
  
[Ron: 2 AM - 5 PM Eastern. That is "through" New York session. However, some folks *might* say the first 4 hours of each session (generally) is good enough.]  
  
This system is just pure price action, if buyers pushed the price up in the past hour, its more likely buyers will push the price up again on the next hour, vice versa for sellers.  
  
However Tony says in more recent post about times to trade from 7 GMT - max of 20 GMT...I believe that is about 2 AM - 3 PM Eastern...is that about right? 2 hours shy of end of NY session?  
  
Hope this helps & not hinders.  
  
Ron

> [Quoting mikkom](/thread/post/2776323#post2776323 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Here is USDJPY with **very** simple rules and h1 (please confirm if I understood the first post correctly) I don't have long m1 data for usdjpy so this is not as reliable as it should be.  
>    
>  Bull candle: previous candle must be a "good" bull candle, open is at lower 25% of the candle and close is at upper 25% of the candle. Vice versa for bear candles.  
>    
>  I enter at new bar open + (- for shorts) 10 pips (with buy/sell stop) and target 20 pips (with tp). Stop loss is always at previous candle low.  
>    
>  Note that I don't use any indicators here, just...
> 
> Ignored

  
Your EA is not functioning correctly, you are only achieving a 46% accuracy, any thing less than 85% is pointless for backtesting, irrelevant of the availability of the data, i have data that goes back to 2005, when you get it running smoothly, i can run it through if you'd like.

Hi MPP  
  
LOL i love em. I did take 2 trades on this system, but added my little swing to it by having TP at 1:1 for half my position and let the other half run. Same set up that I use for my IB trades in my journal. Both got a little steam before coming back and knocking me out. What I look for is bigger R/R and this method suits that to a T because the small risk means small movement to 1:1, after that its a free ride. Some candles today which I missed (looking at my own system 99% of the time) ran extremely nicely, in some cases ran passed 5:1 R/R. The ultimate benefit could be what I look for an that is a trade that runs for much longer and yields a much greater R/R. It is possible to let your winners run longer than 20 pips if some are prepared, but that is not part of this method so I dont want to take away the core which is outlined in the first few post.  
  
Take care   
  
Razor

Sorry tony_dtrader,   
  
I just want to add something about the 'being greedy' part (MPP). Just adding that aiming for more pips on a single trade is smart business. Greedy can be alot of things (I know this is not what your referring to MPP bud) but letting some winners run past X point can do wonders for your equity curve and your account balance. I trade the more volitile pair of GBP/USD especially during the London/New york cross. It offers good moves, and if you get a small risk candle you can maximise your potential by letting it run.  
  
How you do that is up to you. You could move your SL to +5 after say 20 pips, and if you weather the storm you could make greater pips. I post a pic of the GBP to show you what I mean. By doing this you can also alleviate the amount of time spent at your screen.  
  
If this is stepping over the boundaries tony_dtrader just let me know and Ill remove this post (dont want to step on toes of someone elses methods)  
  
Take care   
  
Razor

Just looking at the new threads I came upon Tony_ dtrader and his simple method. I made a chart of all the entries I saw using his 1m template. The 7 entries today made 20 pips each depending if you could patiently hold two of them over an hour. One of those had 14 pips drawdown which is a loss for some folks. The other 5 paid within the hour. Seems a 10 pip stop, b/e at +10 with a 10 pip trailing stop might be a good money management plan. Just my opinion from initial observation.  
  
Anyhow, an easy 80+ pips during the time I trade today near New York timezone.  
  
Thanks for an interesting simple concept.

Also Stevewise  
  
neither of these methods are what i conside to be greedy, they are controlled methods of trade management, the greed comes in when poeple start trying aim for 100pips each time, suddenly there in massive drawdowns even with a small SL position - WHY, well because the system looks to me to be geared towards trading the momentum factor and has no bearing on the actual trend - so aim to high and it will kick you good and hard  
  
TP 1 half at position X and letting the rest run and trailing it wll take some control but seem to me to be an excellent option, a simple low MA (ie 5) would i expect easily increase the odds of far higher gains on the second position  
  
But for now lets let Tony teach his way, after all he may have tried all these ideas.

  * [#127](/thread/post/2783725#post2783725 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 6, 2009 6:28am  Jun 6, 2009 6:28am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar39214_4.gif) apfx](apfx)

  * | Joined May 2007  | Status: Trader | [75 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=39214)

here is AFL (Amibroker Formula Language) Code :  
The bodyfactor argument controls the minimum accepted size of candle's body as a fraction of high-low range.  
The rangefactor argument controls the minimum accepted size of candle's body compared to 15-bar simple moving average of |close-open| range.  
  

Inserted Code
    
    
    bodyfactor = param("BF", 20, 10 , 90, 20)/100;
    rangefactor = param("RF", 100, 100 , 200, 20)/100;
    
    Buy = CdWhite(bodyfactor,rangefactor );
    Short = CdBlack(bodyfactor,rangefactor);
    Sell = Cover = 0;
    
    //PositionScore = 100 * mtRandomA(); 
    

    Plot( C, "", colorWhite, styleBar );
    PlotShapes( Buy* shapeSmallUpTriangle, colorGreen, 0, L );
    PlotShapes( Short* shapeSmallDownTriangle, colorRed, 0, H );
    
    
    
    /* Backtester Settings*/
    SetOption( "initialequity", 100 );
    SetOption( "FuturesMode" , 1);
    SetOption( "ActivateStopsImmediately", 0 );
    SetOption( "Allowsamebarexit", 0 );
    SetOption( "PriceBoundChecking", 0 );
    SetBacktestMode(backtestRegular);
    
    PointValue = 1;
    MarginDeposit = -2;
    /* Exit*/
    stp = 1.5* ATR(10);
    tKp = 0.2*ATR(10);
    ApplyStop( stopTypeLoss, stopModePoint, stp, 1 );
    ApplyStop( stopTypeProfit, stopModePoint , tKp, 1 );
    
    SetPositionSize( 5 , spsPercentOfEquity );

Attached File(s)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Getting closer to ...... | [1,787 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96744)

Spot on, that is why I have respect for you. The setting of unrealistic goals (100 pips in a market of currencies may not seem like much) forces traders to spend far to long looking, monitoring and adjusting there trades. When you start to set goals, you start to chase your tail, by that I mean if 100 pips a day is your goal and you have 2 lossers for 20 pips each, suddenly your goal is 140 so you ultimatly sit there are rack out trades trying to make up for the loss. Let the market do as it will. It is simply an opportunity flow. Some days you will make nothing, others you will make up for it.  
  
You need to understand trading as a business, not a day job. If you look at each day as a day where you have to make money then you are going to stress yourself to a point of exhaustion.  
  
Thanks MPP  
  
Razor

And looking at your chart the first thing I will do is revert back to a previous comment about being able to withstand the small pullbacks, get to 1:1 and let the trade run. The first trade would have still being running (pending further charts) which was over 100 pips on your first trade, and all you where looking for was 1:1 or there abouts and letting the trade do its thing. The other point I make is that after that first trade went 1:1 and you took some profit, it would have freed up some margin and you could have added some more along the way if you chose.  
  
None of this is considered greed. All you are doing is taking the options that the market is giving you to maximise your account growth. You could quite easily stop at the first trade and see how it pans out. Positive pips is positive growth.  
  
Take care all, have a good weekend  
  
Razor

  * [#135](/thread/post/2784258#post2784258 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 9:51pm  Jun 6, 2009 9:22pm | Edited 9:51pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar39214_4.gif) apfx](apfx)

  * | Joined May 2007  | Status: Trader | [75 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=39214)

> [Quoting fugly](/thread/post/2784102#post2784102 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> can you paste the body factor and range factor parameter options (what the options are) from your amibroker BF and RF funtion library help file? So we can understand better.
> 
> Ignored

bodyfactor and rangefactor are the arguments for the candlestick functions generated by AB candlesitck functions plugin (candle.dll).   
  
All functions have "Cd" prefix appended to avoid name conflicts with built-in functions.  
  
CdWhite( bodyfactor = 0.4, rangefactor = 0) - returns True (1) when white candle appears, False (0) otherwise.  
CdBigWhite( bodyfactor = 0.9, rangefactor = 1.5) - returns True (1) when a big white candle appears, False (0) otherwise.  
CdBlack( bodyfactor = 0.4, rangefactor = 0) - returns True (1) when black candle appears, False (0) otherwise.  
CdBigBlack( bodyfactor = 0.9, rangefactor = 1.5) - returns True (1) when a big black candle appears, False (0) otherwise.  
CdDoji( threshold = 0.05 ) - returns True (1) when doji is detected, False (0) otherwise. The threshold argument defines maximum allowed difference between open and close as a fraction of high-low range.  
CdHammer( rangefactor= 1.1 ) - returns True (1) when hammer is detected, False (0) otherwise. This function checks if Close is higher than half the distance between high and low and the candle is black. In addition to that the body size of the candle must be greater rangefactor * average |close-open| range from 15 bars, and open has to be located not lower than 10% of candle height from the high price.  
CdBearishEngulfing( bodyfactor = 0.4, rangefactor = 0.5) returns True (1) when Bearish engulfing pattern is detected, False (0) otherwise.  
CdBullishEngulfing( bodyfactor = 0.4, rangefactor = 0.5) returns True (1) when Bullish engulfing pattern is detected, False (0) otherwise.  
  
bodyfactor = ( close - open )/ (high-low);  
rangefactor = (close - open)/ MA ( (close-open), 15);  
* absolute values  
  

> [Quoting fugly](/thread/post/2784102#post2784102 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Also am I correct in assuming your stop is 7 times your take profit. also what does positionscore mean?
> 
> Ignored

Yes, stop loss must be greater than take profit.   
  
PositionScore = 100 * mtRandomA(); - is for picking randomly the trade signals out of the total number of generated signals for portfolio backtesting.

> Disliked

> i already test this system. i think the system won't work in ranging market. most of the time it hits the SL than TP. I think with 1H timeframe, the 10-20 SL is too small. any response for this. I appreciate for all of the response. thx
> 
> Ignored

  
10-20 pips is not the SL - it's the target, the stop is at the end of the indicator candle, if the next candle fails to make the TP and turns around you have choices  
  
ie   
first indicator candle is long - tp 10pips on half, second half to BE if first half hit, stop at low of indicator candle ie 50pips  
  
Tp not hit candle closes bearish, but stop not hit - exit trade wait for next candle to show, this candle become a bearish (short) indicator candle  
  
next trade short tp 10pips etc  
  
stop and reverse and so on.

No problems,  
  
I know there are better systems available, there are bound to be. On this Forum there must be thousands. Most systems stem from someone elses workings, are tweak and distorded over time. Few are completely unique. My reference was based on something that is all too common on trading forums, and that is imput on systems that provides little benefit to those who are taking the time to trial it.  
  
If something doesnt look good to someone then they should just bit there tongue, or make the relevant comments and move on. I have made my comments and at times used specific examples or where I feel the wording should be different (the 100K post only 2 pages back is an example). The only time something should be frowned upon heavily is when there is a genuine risk of new traders following something, or joining something that is never going to work.   
  
All in all, longevity is a key to determining success traders and is also a way of determining successful systems. Threads that gain momentum and last past 200 plus pages with a number of people enjoying success can in the end have credit in my book, regardless of how some people percieve the short or long term success of that system.  
  
I guess in time we will find out just how well this works out.  
  
Also as I have mentioned, a system doesnt need to be 50%+ to be successful. If a trader can eclipse the mental barrier of just trading for 2:1 or 1:1 then s/he can unlock a door that allows huge gains of single mediocre setups. Its rare, but possible. I trade for this, just like Joel Rensink and Peter Crowns. I trade with a small group live and we have been having great success with some traders this week making over 5:1 R/R and some cases 10:1. Sometimes the setups seem simple and therefore people associate simple results, move past this and there are ample opportunities to hold singular trades for much longer than the average.  
  
Take care, my apologies at the rashness of the previous post.  
  
Razor

> [Quoting redpine](/thread/post/2785135#post2785135 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Interesting idea. However, if you look at historical data, the probabilities with hourly bars is the same as with daily bars. The chance the that the next bar is the same direction is a coin flip, with a slightly improved probability going to the expectation that the bar will go the opposite direction.
> 
> Ignored

Historical data - yes when you look at each bar, very few are in the same direction - nothing new there, thats not what this method looks for.  
  
look at the wicks - how many made it past entry plus 10/20pips before changing direction  
  
Momentum/round numbers/fib points/ma - most traders use these and base there trading on things like this, therefore we have wicks - why, because of the buyers/sellers targets for entry and exits, this allows price to move beyond the close of the previous bar - that's why this method has potential  
  
Richard Farleigh - taming the lion, in his book he talks about trading with the masses, when price changes by around 10% either way get on board and go with the flow - he's a dam sight richer than most and no indicators  
  
simple as that  
  
try it for a few months.

  * Jun 8, 2009 6:36am  Jun 8, 2009 6:36am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar71402_5.gif) redpine](redpine)

  * | Joined Jun 2008  | Status: Trader | [84 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=71402)

> [Quoting MPP](/thread/post/2785155#post2785155 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Historical data - yes when you look at each bar, very few are in the same direction - nothing new there, thats not what this method looks for.  
>    
>  look at the wicks - how many made it past entry plus 10/20pips before changing direction  
>    
>  Momentum/round numbers/fib points/ma - most traders use these and base there trading on things like this, therefore we have wicks - why, because of the buyers/sellers targets for entry and exits, this allows price to move beyond the close of the previous bar - that's why this method has potential  
>    
>  Richard Farleigh...
> 
> Ignored

I'm sure you have something but the original poster stated 99% accuracy with just one bar.   
  
I trade a slight variation based upon reversals and inner bars for the daily timeframe. It has a 61% win/loss over 21 pairs and makes about 1000 pips a month. In live trading real money for two month I've gotten 65% win/loss and 1900 pips in two months. The only indicator is a regression slope.   
  
I started with DIBS which can not be validated in backtesting, but discovered a few things looking at historical data. An inner bar is more likely to reverse and the best days to close a position is either the third or fifth (probably similar results would hold for hourly bars). The second and fourth days have a greater chance of reversing, historically speaking. Oh ya another thing is the sanctity of an inner bar holds no relevance for the reverse. For a long position the inner bar breaking the lower bound of the outer bar has no importance. In fact a breakout from that pattern has a higher probability of success.  
  
So the thing I typically do do is look at which patterns play out with this system. Have you looked at any probabilities of wicks and their impact or is this anecdotal evidence as is provided in the start?  
  
Sorry if I came of criticizing the system but I like to start with the odds in my favor. Has anyone looked at how this would play out with a reversal of the direction in the next bar? A reversal is more likely. 

.

  * [#162](/thread/post/2785850#post2785850 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 8, 2009 9:48am  Jun 8, 2009 9:48am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar96744_2.gif) Razor_trader](razor_trader)

  * Joined Mar 2009 | Status: Getting closer to ...... | [1,787 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=96744)

I am going to make 2 more posts on this thread, and perhaps forget about my journal aswell.  
  
The problem with ALL factory threads is that there are a few people out there who are genuinly trying to succeed and then there are others who just have to come along and try to ruin the flow.  
  
The information given in any particular arena can be tossed and turned until the beliefs of a few can overwhelm the beliefs of many. In most instances the person who started a particular thread gets fed up and moves away to enjoy or lament their future. So many threads that have been started by a particular person seldom see that person actively post throughout the entire thread, in fact they can go weeks or months without posting. This leads one to think a few things. They are either enjoying there success with the orginal method or they have gone bust and dont want to show themselves for fear of looking like a failure. The second to most is probably the prominant truth.  
  
When I came along I was just genuinly interested in the simplicity of this thread. The orginal post and subsequent posts could have been tweaked slightly as the claims may not be quite as high (MY BELIEF) so I stated so, but that statement was made once. I then went on to provide some support. However, Tony may have been trading this method for years, he may have found an EDGE to this method that he perhaps doesnt want to share right now. Believe it or not (even in randomness) traders who have devoted a particular amount of time to something with usually always see more information in particular circumstances that would trigger alarms. These alarms may be a load up situation or a hold back situation. These situations, no matter how well they try to define them to others will seldom be absorbed until they have spent time trading and can see it.  
  
Very few people understand FOREX and most come along because today it is advertised like a monster on the internet. Proven methods, demo accounts with 100K leveraged a 400:1 promising money, auto traders that trade for you, the list goes on and on and ON. 4 years ago when I started trading there was much much less on the internet in ways of adverts. If you wanted to find something there was stacks of information, but you had to have some idea as to what it is you wanted. Youtube holds thousands of 'winning strategy' vids that people can watch. Very few people truly understand the risks of trading. They come along to forums, watch countless videos and try to participate without understanding. Does it take a great deal of knowledge to understand trading? Not neccesarily otherwise the uber minds of the world would be dominating this business.   
  
Why do 95% of people fail. There are a number of reasons. In most cases it is there desire to make millions out of cents in the shortest time and without devoting enough time to see if some particular thing works. That brings me back to the countless times (in all threads) where an anon person make a pointless claim that something they refuse to give anytime to will fail. How easy is it to do! It is easy for people to put in there 2c, walk away and never be seen again. Most times you can look back upon this 'posters' previous posts and find support immediatly in that they have seldom contributed to any thread more than a handful of times.   
  
Forums like these are at there core designed to be a place where people can have access to information. People come up with an idea ( currently working or in the process of) and post it. They give out the information they feel relative and other come along and give there imput. Imput is great if people understand the initial post. If they dont then they simple ask for it and in time the thread initiator will give it. These people are the constructive ones, they are looking at something, deeming it to be possible but just need to get some more pieces of the puzzle. In time most of these will give this method a go and if things work out for the better then the posts will thrive and thread will grow to a point where the information gathered will vastly outweigh the critism that rogue posters deliver.   
  
Final note: We all have the desire to succeed but desire isnt enough. Traders take years and years of hard knocks before finally putting all the pieces together. Few people have the time to withstand this. Few people have the time to read, understand and implement. I can back this up with the mountains of posters who make the rediculous claims without proof that something doesnt work. They open a thread, go straight to the last page and ask how something works, they are not prepared to go back through the pages and pages of posts to get answers to the questions that have been raised tens to hundreds of times. Some just read the opening post and make judgement. These are the same people who (if they read books at all) just read a blurb and decide that a book contains nothing useful or no great storyline. I dont normally worry myself with these people because the vast majority will not get past there first 100 trades (or less) without disaster and that will be there trading career gone in the blink of an eye.   
  
A trader, a successful trader will weather the storm. They take the hits, understand them and still move forward. These very few understand that there are great times, and there are not so great times. They understand that trading is risk and riskless trading doesnt exist. All strategies have limitations and therefore all strategies will reach points where they dont work aswell as they were. Traders know this and they can adapt. Longevity is one of the keystones of trading. The longevity to be in the game for the years to decades will mean perservering through the hard times to come out the end and go again. Successful traders can still BLOWUP, but they get back on there feet. They can be part of the 5% crowd, loss all and start again. The 95% crowd doesnt achieve the above because they cannot accept it. Some look to blame. They blame the markets for not doing what it should have done, they blame a thread starter for starting something that didnt work for THEM, they blame everyone and everything without understanding what they did. Because of the emotional pain and not being able to rationally digest it they walk away to a full time job that earns them there EXPECTED pay packet every week.  
  
I do not claim to be an uber successful trader, I do however understand everything I have written. I have been in this game for 4 years now, have placed a good number of trades, come close to blowing an account and then rebuilt it. I too at my early stages limbo'd from method to method before the spark went off in my head that what I was doing was causing the backwardness in my trading. At that point I stopped myself. I started taking a more Proactive approach to not only trading, but to understanding why I want to trade and how I could further that understanding. Ive had the AH HA moments in the shorter past that has made me a better individual trader.   
  
I am disapointed, but not at all suprised by what happens in these forums. I am glad to see that there are still many out there who are prepared to take the time to learn, understand and implement an idea to see if it is possibly credible and then start giving feedback. To the others, go on doing what you do best and provide the liquidity for those who are prepared to take the time to trade.  
  
There may be a few responses to this post and I may read them but I doubt I will take any action because the ones who respond to it in there manner will obviously taken it personally which seems to be a fundamental flaw.  
  
Take care  
  
Razor

I read somewhere that the first 15 min is where the volume is. Some people tell you on here not to change things. I agree. But i like to think outside of the box.  
  
  
This thread does seem kind of low today.  
  
Look at post 170, 173. Thats the way i trade it. It recommended to use slow currencies.   
  
At the end of every hour i look at the currencies and see what the high and low says at that time. I draw the trend line on the 1 hour and 30 min candles. If it is bouncing of a trend line thats how i enter.   
  
The 4 oclock candle has been the best for the last 2 days. The 8 oclock candle has also been a good time to trade.   
  
I read somewhere that the first 15 min is where the volume is.  
  
Some people tell you on here not to change things. I agree. But i like to think outside of the box.  
  
I also watch for announcements coming out. If im in a trade i always tighten up my stop loss. This is a good thread.   
  
Typing is not my thing, even though i took it in school.  
  
I wish eveyone well.  
  
SMURF

Look to see if the close of the previous candle is above/below the 12 high/low EMA.  
  
What I found was that the EA worked best for the month of March. I think the reason why is because there was very little volatility during that month (this is when all the stock markets bottomed out). I tried fooling around with a volatility based indicator - the standard deviation envelope, but it didn't lead to any improvement. Then I played around with Tony's high/low MA idea by optimizing and the 12 high/low EMA worked best.   
  
What I need is a volatility based indicator that is normalized. Something like ATR (only that indicator isn't normalized). 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#199](/thread/post/2801403#post2801403 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 14, 2009 8:13pm  Jun 14, 2009 8:13pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar64560_4.gif) Danoid](danoid)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [56 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=64560)

Let me rephrase that - I need a way of normalizing the ATR (since a non-native indicator will take a long time to optimize). 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#200](/thread/post/2802163#post2802163 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 15, 2009 10:22am  Jun 15, 2009 10:22am 

  * [ fxxx](fxxx)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Trader | [475 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=55426)

here's universal normalizer ind.  
type-in exact ind filename, you want to normalize, param, ind. middle level - go  
like: atr, 14, 0,0,0, midlevel- 0.007  
macd, 12,26,9, mid:0;  
rsi:14,0,0,50 etc

>  Now simply wait for a bull or bear candle to form, after it closes bullish or bearish, its most likely the next candle will form bull or bear candle...theres some easy pips for you.  
>    
>  Examples:   
>    
>  Bull candle at 8gmt, most likely 9gmt candle could be a bull candle too.  
>  Bear candle at 11gmt, most likely 12gmt candle could be a bear too.  
>    
>  Entry exit rules:  
>  Bull candle --- stoploss at the low of the previous candle,...

#  [](/thread/172963-tonys-two-candle-trading-system)Tony's Two Candle trading system 

  * 

  * [#221](/thread/post/2837315#post2837315 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 30, 2009 3:11am  Jun 30, 2009 3:11am 

  * [ gez40](gez40)

  * | Joined May 2009  | Status: Trader | [557 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=104470)

This is one of the ways i`ve been trading for about 4yrs, not sure why some people are being so negative about it, you are simply using the high of the previous bar as your entry and taking some pips.  
  
My set up is this:  
  
1hr candles  
14 sma  
Direction of the sma determines buy or sell, if the sma is pointing up we look for buy set ups, opposite for shorts. Once the current candle closes we simply use the next candle to push through the high for a long entry, as long as the previous bar was bullish and the sma was up, opposite for shorts using the low of the previos bear candle.  
  
Thats it, it was a system used by a trader called shiraz, i think i got around 02/03 time, the formula was called CTF ( champion trader formula), like i said, not my normal stratergy but it works pretty well for a few pips.  
  
Gez 

Seek not to change the world; seek only to change your mind about the world

Hi there,  
  
I`ve been reading this thread since yesterday and just made a quiq back test on E/U - one trade / day, at london open.  
  
Sice 13 may till today, i saw that in 25 situations the candle from london open, had the same color as the one before it, generating profit. Also, in 10 situations, observing the wicks, it might of looked like a continuation of the prior bar, validating a buy / sell signal, only for the price to go in the oposit direction, generating losses.  
  
This is only a quick visual test. I`ll be testing some more.

  * Jul 14, 2009 3:44am  Jul 14, 2009 3:44am 

  * [ pimind](pimind)

  * | Joined Mar 2009  | Status: Trader | [5 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=95782)

I have not read the whole thread so this might have already been covered.  
  
I have used a similar system for years in forex and other markets . This system is profitable if you use common sense and discretion.  
  
I believe tony is trying to make 20-40 pips per day. so its about 2-3 trades. If you trade overlap sessions then you have approx. 7-10 good candles to trade. If you follow a few pairs then you have at least 30-40 apportunities per day.   
  
So pick the best ones. Use filters.   
  
I use the following:  
simple moving averages, a 9 period for trend for example, don't trade against trend.  
I also look at candle formations and take hammers etc,.  
  
my point is that any system can be simple, but some discretion and trading knowledge is needed even with the simplest system.  
  
If you blindly follow the rules and actually follow them 100% then you will not do any better than an automated system.  
  
this is my opinion for what its worth.

#  [](/thread/172963-tonys-two-candle-trading-system)Tony's Two Candle trading system 

  * 

  * [#241](/thread/post/2880206#post2880206 "Post Permalink")

  * Jul 17, 2009 9:42am  Jul 17, 2009 9:42am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar64560_4.gif) Danoid](danoid)

  * | Joined Mar 2008  | Status: Trader | [56 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=64560)

The rules aren't any different than Tony's rules, except for the addition of the 12 Hi/Low EMAs, PSAR (with a setting of .03), AO, and ADX (with a setting of 2).  
  
For going long: Close of last bar is above the 12 Hi EMA, price > PSAR, AO of 1 hour ago is > AO of 2 hours ago, and ADX of 1 hour ago is > ADX of 2 hours ago.  
  
For going short: Close of last bar is below the 12 Low EMA, price < PSAR, AO of 1 hour ago is < AO of 2 hours ago, and ADX of 1 hour ago is > ADX of 2 hours ago.   
  
In other news, my EA made 3 losing trades that wiped out all my gains...so perhaps this isn't my holy grail after all. I have it set to make only one trade per day now (...greed is the downfall of this trading method!).  
  
Optimal trading time for that one trade appears to be from 9:00 am to 3:00 pm EST.

thanks 4 pdf  
  

**PREDICTING PRICE ACTION: USDJPY 15 pip trigger**  
When price moves 15 pips in either direction, what is the probability that it will continue to the following values with the currency and interval shown?   
_For example, when USDJPY moves 15 pips up or down on the 5 minute interval, the probability that it will continue to +80 (+65 net) is 4.0%._  
**PAIR: USDJPY**

  

**INTERVAL: 60 MINUTE CHART**  
**+20**  
**+30**  
**+40**  
**+50**  
**+60**  
**+70**  
**+80**  
**+90**  
**+100+**  
91.6%   
72.9%   
58.9%   
47.8%   
37.4%   
30.5%   
24.3%   
19.0%   
14.9%

> **PREDICTING PRICE ACTION: USDJPY 15 pip trigger**  
>  When price moves 15 pips in either direction, what is the probability that it will continue to the following values with the currency and interval shown?   
>  _For example, when USDJPY moves 15 pips up or down on the 5 minute interval, the probability that it will continue to +80 (+65 net) is 4.0%._  
>  **PAIR: USDJPY**
> 
>   
>  [left][b][size=2]INTERVAL: 60...
> 
> Ignored

are you saying there is a 91.6% chance of positive pips after the pair moves 15 pips  
so if I place a buy stop 15 pips at previous high or sell stop previous low I   
have a 91.6% of making pips on a 60 min chart or 5 min chart  
  
just trying to understand what you are saying here

Hello all,  
  
Just thought I would drop a note and say thanks to Tony for such a simple and effective system and sharing it to the FF community.  
  
I am using this system with some small changes and am having a reasonable amount of success thus far.   
  
As far as the Pairs I am using I started with uds/jpy as Tony suggested and then moved to eur/jpy as it seemed to have more price movement with out an unmanageable amount of volatility.  
  
Time frames? I have been trading this method beginning at the Asian open and ending around mid way through the us session..  
  
I use an initial 15 pip stop and take profit depends on PA. And its important to mention that the Stop depends on PA also.. Yes, initial is 15 pips but if the trade is entered and the PA stalls I will exit at a small loss or small profit..  
  
I also Size my trades according to PA and/or if I recently had a huge winner on a large position.. or a string of 2-3 winners in a row..I will decrease my Size by 2/3..  
  
Thanks again Tony!  
  
399BC

  * [ dannywmk](dannywmk)

  * | Joined Jun 2008  | Status: Trader | [46 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=72910)

so, viewing a static chart you will notice 90% of time a 2nd bull bar will have a high 20 pips above the 1st bull bar's high (and vice versa for bear bars), but from a dynamic point of view (looking at tick chart, looking the price in action), what is the chance that the price will hit the 20pips TP instead of the 5~10pips (mental) stop loss?   
  
fact is, SL will be hit more often than the TP bcoz (1) price will likely retrace a bit and testing the breakout and (2) from the distance of the TP and the SL, ie. 20 : 10, it is obvious that chance of SL being hit is 2 times higher than the TP being hit.

> 
> Disliked
> 
> How big SL do you guys use?

> 
> Ignored

hey, hoichoi  
  
At the time of candle close, I set pending entry for 4 pips above/below close price (if it is long, add the spread, since trade will open at the ask line)   
  
I start at 20 pip stop, but that is only temporary to avoid disaster. If I am in front of the screen and trade opens, I start moving the stop down a few pips at a time as the price moves in my favor.   
  
I set target at 20, but if in front of screen, usually close trade myself if price seems to stall anywhere along the way.  
  
often, begin to manually trail stop when profit reaches 8-10 pips but usually only score a few pips that way.  
  
The big problem with this way is this. . . taking so many tiny profits, will almost inevitably cause loss of all profits with just one or two 20 pip losses. Even a success rate of 90% will be mostly wiped out with one 15 or 20 pip loss  
  
One GOOD thing about this system: many of your losers NEVER EVEN OPEN, thus avoid loss.   
  
Sometimes the best trade is to not trade at all.  
  
Shakey 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

The minute chart has always been too quick for me to digest. I mostly flip back to the 5 min. There will possibly be up to 12 5 min candles during your trade period.   
  
Pretty much watch to see if POSSIBLE reversal candle is happing, like a hammer/shooting star forming, or possible higher high, lower low.   
  
This is dicey, because you will have to close trade before complete pattern is formed, and therefore, might leave a lot of money on the table/  
  
IT MAY BE JUST AS WELL TO SET UP THE TRADE, LET IT OPEN, IGNORE IT, CLOSE IT AFTER AN HOUR (if it hasn't stopped or reached it's target already) AND TAKE YOUR PROFIT/LOSS.  
  
Despite early success, I have doubts about the system, and whether a person can be consistent enough with having to manipulate so much for so long.  
  
I do use a couple of filters, which I can tell you about later when have time.  
  
Shakey

> [Quoting PennFX](/thread/post/3505770#post3505770 "View Quoted Post")

Here is a sample pic, Sorry, I didn't have a sample of actual trade, so I admit that this example is cherry picked.  
  
I like the basic concept of this system. Tony has put a lot of time and study into this system, and appreciate him putting out there for us ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)  
  
Basically, I have had some success adding these indicators, though I am usually not an idicator junkie.  
  
The pivots and currency meter can be found <http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=219398> , or at least links to them.  
  
A word about the currency meter: **I will not discuss this meter, nor include a link directly to it. You can find a discussion of it at the link provided above.**  
  
1\. add 5 moving average to chart. The signal candle should cut across the 5 ma. Usually, the price will challenge the 5 ma, at some point, before continuing the long/short move.  
  
2\. Add the 34 MA to chart. If price is above 34, take only long, below only short (Ignore the fact that in my example, the trade happens on an MA cross, This is just a coincidence) (_It just now dawned on me that an MA cross might be a good additional filter)._  
  
3\. Note that signal candle has short wick. May indicate good momentum. Also a pinbar makes a good signal candle.  
  
4\. I have been moving stop to break even at 6 pips profit.  
  
5\. Nearby Pivots and round numbers make good targets, if you are insecure about the 10 or 20 pip targes that are recommended.  
  
6\. on currency meter, Note that USD is stronger than JPY.  
  
I have also had some luck with this on the AU and UCad pairs during the european session.   
  
If profits taken are too small, one 20 pip stoploss can wipe out a day's work in a flash. I have made a little profit from it over all, but I have a tendency to micro manage.   
  
Hope some of this helps, and hope Tony doesn't feel I have screwed up his system.  
  
Shakey

  * Edited Jun 7, 2010 12:59am  Jun 6, 2010 5:51pm | Edited Jun 7, 2010 12:59am 

  * [ nightpipper](nightpipper)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Trader | [79 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=55867)

Hi all,  
  
I am about to test live the following which is very similar to tonys system with a few changes, take a look (unable to upload pics at present so will discribe the best i can.  
  
1/ open up a 15min chart with candles only. (get rid of all clutter eg graph lines )  
  
2/ add a 5 / 8ma crossover indicator with alert (change 5 & 8 to 1 & 2) (search FF and you will find )this will only add directional arrows no lines)  
  
And there you have it - go back in history and just LOOK !!!  
  
My Additions are :  
  
Entry = instantly as new bar opens.  
Exit = ATR or close of next candle.  
SL = High or low of last candle.  
  
I think you should be able to make an average of 15 pips per trade with a better win lose ratio.  
  
I also think using the 1hr Time frame tonys is using could be more profitable if using the ATR as above.  
  
Thanks  
Hope this helps !!!!!!!!!!

Picture explained.  
  
Note i am only viewing from this picture so exact figures are not shown + ATR is not available. ( will explain later how to look back in history )  
  
Here goes, starting from left hand side.  
  
Trade 1 - up arrow-green signal candle- on close of this bar enter your buy trade - your SL=low of the signal bar-enter your TP=ATR - await the close of bar - If Tp & SL have not been touched close trade. In this case without ATR it looks as if the trade broke even.  
  
Trade 2 - up-without ATR made a loss  
Trade 3 - up " " profit  
Trade 4 - up " " profit  
Trade 5 - down" " Profit  
Trade 6 - up " " Loss  
Trade 7 - down " " Profit  
Trade 8 - up " " Profit  
Trade 9 - down " " Profit  
Trade 10 -up " " Profit  
  
I hope this helps !!!  
  
Nightpipper

The thing i like about this system is that instead of waiting all day on a trend system for good signal to make 70 pips, you can more than match that in a matter of a couple of hours.  
Im sure i am not the only one who has tried the many trend systems out there, but as they say the market travel sideways most of the time , so this is the ideal situation for us .   
I have breifly looked at ofter time frames and they all seem to work pretty well up to the 1hr time frame after that it seems to get a bit ramdom. but if anyone can test these and others TFs please let us know how you progress.

  * [#289](/thread/post/3784774#post3784774 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 8, 2010 2:03pm  Jun 8, 2010 2:03pm 

  * [ nightpipper](nightpipper)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Trader | [79 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=55867)

Hi all,  
  
Visual testing for a demo/live chart .  
  
1/ I personally install 2x ATRs 1 set at 5 bars back other set at 20 bars back.  
  
Install the first ATR into its own window as normal - go into its parameters and set 'style' to none this will then turn of the line graph and you will only have the reading of the ATR on the top of the page.  
The for your next ATR drag it from the navigator listing onto the first ATR panel you installed and again turn of the graph as above .  
There you have you existing ATR readings.  
But not these are only showing the existing readings not the historical.  
  
2/ Historical readings of ATR.   
Simply click on Data window icon at top of page - give it time to load - you will then be able to see the 2 x ATR reading you have just installed at the bottom of the listings.  
As you move your curser on screen you can now seethe historical readings of the ATR for each candle.   
  
Sorry if i am tell some of you how to suck eggs ,but it took me some time to find these simple methods so i hope it helps someone out there, in visually back testing.  
  
All the best  
  
Nightpipper.

  * [#298](/thread/post/3787135#post3787135 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 8:55am  Jun 9, 2010 5:02am | Edited 8:55am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar26359_11.gif) chazbo 3071](chazbo*3071)

  * | Joined Nov 2006  | Status: Fightin' Gator | [121 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=26359)

Trading with the slope of the 20 SMA (BB center line), the steeper the better, might offer 2 advantages:  
  
1\. Higher probability of winning trades  
  
2\. These trades have the potential of going for alot more pips than 1xATR. You would have the option of opening 2 positions. The first one 1xATR, second position 2xATR or let it run trailing stop loss.  
  
With the BB, you could also look for reversal patterns (engulfing, long wicks etc.) at outer bands. 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 2.gif
Size: 63 KB](/attachment/image/487514/thumbnail?d=1365634130)](/attachment/image/487514?d=1276026757)   

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#299](/thread/post/3787516#post3787516 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 9, 2010 8:45am  Jun 9, 2010 8:45am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar26359_11.gif) chazbo 3071](chazbo*3071)

  * | Joined Nov 2006  | Status: Fightin' Gator | [121 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=26359)

If you trade against the slope (trend), you can put probabality in your favor with divergence. I'm usually not a fan of MA crossovers, but I'm liking this simple strategy. I hope I haven't complicated it too much.  
  
In addition to the counter slope trades, look at the nice runs trading with the steep slope.

Ok here's a pic.  
  
ignore big blue and purple arrows and squiggly blue line and the Demark lines. they belong to different trials which i don't want to go into.  
  
I have ADX at 9. when +DI line (green) goes through -DI line (red) it indicates a change in trend to BUY (up). pink squares.  
when this line >20 its a stronger trend, when it passes ADX gray line it very strong trend up.  
  
Reverse for SELL (black squares)  
  
this is just an observation and trying this in real time may be different.  
  
Note the MAcrossover alert (little red and blue arrows) are sometimes wrong. I've circled these pink.

  * [ izzysdad](izzysdad)

  * | Joined Jun 2010  | Status: Trader | [3 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=144696)

New to FF so thanks for having me.   
  
I started reading this thread about 2 nights ago (I have only been through the first 7 pages so the conversation may have changed direction), but I thought it would be interesting to "forward test" throughout the day at work when I had a few minutes.  
  
I captured the screen shot below at about 0840 EST (1240 GMT). Times on the chart are EST (GMT-4). The breakout boxes are from the EU 5M TF. White arrows are entry and yellow arrows are TP. (Note: The data is not from a broker but from CMS FOREX.....I can't get to my broker at work).  
  
If you sat down to your computer at 0300 EST (0700 GMT as Tony recommends), used a 10 pip SL / TP, and used the 0300 EST Bull close to trigger your 0400 Bear setup.....you would have a 100% win rate (3 for 3 in 6 hours) through 0900 EST.  
  
Trade 1 is outside of the recommended time period....but a winner.  
  
Trade 2 would have hit the TP exactly to the tenth of a pip. (you probably would have had to use discretion here since it was so tight. It would depend on how many decimal places you can see)  
  
Trade 3 was a winner, but it was deceptive. As you can see in the breakout box. PA ran straight up and hit the TP before retracing.  
  
Trade 4 since the 0700 candle closed bear (slightly) the 0800 then became a setup for a winning trade within the 0900 candle. (the 0900 did retrace after this screen shot, but an easy winner).  
  
I've continued to watch throughout the day (now 1400 EST / 1800 GMT), and there is actually another winner using the 1200 and 1300 EST candles.  
  
That is 4 wins in 4 trades (5 if you count trade 1 which is outside the recommended time period), and if you have Tony's bankroll (enough to trade 50 Lots) you just pocketed $20K.  
  
Not bad.......I'll have to keep an eye on this one.

> Ignored

The reason you see "wrong" sinals is because when the two MAs cross it will show the "signal" on the charts. And if you watch MA crossings they sometimes cross, then "open" back up again and move in its original direction. So this indi leaves a signal when the MAs actually cross (not at the close of the candle) and will leave it there even if the MAs open back up. And then it will leave a signal again at the next crossing. Hope that helps.

I was not able to fully account for the spread when making the chart. My info was not that good (internet feed at work), but going forward I plan to use by broker's data each evening.  
  
That said. IMHO. If a good trader were watching this all happen I think it still would have been a profitable day. Three of them would have won easily (if you assume a 2.5-3 pip spread (including the first trade and the trade in the NY afternoon.......NY afternoon may not have made a full 10, but a close on candle close would have netted most). The other 2 (I can't see them right now, but I think they were trades 2 and 3) could have been closed out as winners if you were watching the 5M during the trade. I think that is particularly true on trade 3 where you can see the hourly high right next to the arrow (in the breakout box) and about 15 minutes later you can see a lower high. You may have wanted to exit at that point (lower high) considering there wasn't that much time left in the hour and you had most of your 10 pips. Trade 2 may have been tough, but even there you would have had to close on candle close. You might have lost 2-3 pips.   
  
After all that, I think you could conservatively say the you would be net positive 15-25 pips.  
  
Like I said.....it can't be that easy. It did look promising though.  
  
Cheers

  * [#316](/thread/post/3791082#post3791082 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 10, 2010 11:27am  Jun 10, 2010 11:27am 

  * [ NiceGuy](niceguy)

  * Joined Apr 2010 | Status: Trader | [971 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=140145)

Helo all...  
  
Been doing observation with this strategy for a couple of days or so and I know that the ATR and ADX is always "too much details" to read for me so I tried different approach. RSI is my favorite.  
  
Please check this out:  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 2Candle-with-RSI5.jpg
Size: 213 KB](/attachment/image/488408/thumbnail?d=1365634351)](/attachment/image/488408?d=1276133951)   

  
  
Chart above is EU H1, [FX Pro](/brokers/fxpro "View FxPro Broker Profile") Demo GMT +2.  
  
**Observation time:** Look for Candle that touch the outer bands or even better when they passed the bands and hits a known resistance or support level. RSI 5 Pass 70 for sell and 30 for buy..   
  
**Trade:** Exactly when you hear the sound of the Green/Red arrow appears. SL at Top or bottom of the same candle with Arrow. (around 10 - 20 pips ussually, but it depends on how soon you enter the trade after you hear the allert).  
  
Been shooting for 10 pips and won. But as you can see that all the trades have a good potential to developed further more with this.   
  
Maybe we can shoot for 20-30(?). Surely I need to find the best exit strategy to define the best time to bail out from the trade. Suggestion needed here.  
  
Those are the good thing, now the bad things.  
If you are not watching the chart all day, you have to be lucky enough to be there when this thing happens. I was lucky enough to get 3 trades in last 2 days.   
  
Won straight 30 pips in 3 trades. Worth it if we play with big lots, but for mini lots I dont know if it's worth the time.  
  
Maybe we can get more signal with less timeframe but I could see that the RSI somehow get less reliable on less time frame(?).   
  
For some of us who dont have much time in front of Computer, maybe we can play this strategy with multiple pairs opened for better chances to get signals and enter when you see one......I dont know...need to test further...![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f914.png?v=15.1)   
  
EA maybe?

  * [ Jhig](jhig)

Arrows? Are you using Arrows/indicator/ea to show you entry? Thats not good.  
  
In the same, this is the exact strategy I use, and have been using for 3 and a half years. It's basically a price action reversal system, using Dark Cloud, Pin Bars (a.k.a Hammers), & Engulfed candlestick formations. Not a complicated system at all, you just have to learn the basic of candlestick reversal patterns. No indicator/ea needed! The idea is to trade high contract position, with as little market exposure as possible. As I've always said, "its easier to make 10 pips than 100 pips"  
  
You're on the right track, just lose the indicators.
