I second that.  
  
Would be nice of Tony to drop in and say hi or something, don't you guys think? Anyways, thanks Tony for the system.  
  
I just wanted to touch the issue of filtering for a sec. A lot of guys here are trying to come up with some sort of a filter to improve the hit rate. I just thought I'll share my idea as well.  
  
From my experience, the best filter is the one that does not lag. Everything you put on your chart (adx, stochs, ma's, etc.) depends on the price itself, so how can it serve as a filter? So, what does not lag then? The price itself, nothing else. So, a good filter would be another timeframe, and only higher timeframe. You only look at lower timeframes to time your entry, and you look at higher timeframes to filter your set up.   
  
Look at my screenshot. There's my H1 timeframe in the middle. Once I see a bullish setup for example (bear-bull-time to enter?) I immediately look at H4 and Daily (the two time frames on the bottom), if H4 is also looking bullish, I have green light, if it doesn't, I look at Daily, if Daily looks bullish, then I might consider taking this setup (though it will not be an A+ setup), then I look at 1min and 5min on the top, my timing time frames, and time my entry, they both have to start looking bullish as well.   
  
This, in my humble opinion, is the best way to filter and time an entry. No need for anything else, just price itself. I do have stochs on the charts as you can see, but they are there mostly for fun, but if stochs are all UP on all timeframes, that adds to the confidence greatly. Some people trade multi-timeframe stochs with great success, but I still believe that price itself is the only real-time, non-lagging thing.

> [Quoting masterpiecefx](/thread/post/3793871#post3793871 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I second that.  
>    
>  From my experience, the best filter is the one that does not lag. Everything you put on your chart (adx, stochs, ma's, etc.) depends on the price itself, so how can it serve as a filter? So, what does not lag then? The price itself, nothing else. So, a good filter would be another timeframe, and only higher timeframe. You only look at lower timeframes to time your entry, and you look at higher timeframes to filter your set up. .
> 
> Ignored

  * [#343](/thread/post/3794699#post3794699 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 11, 2010 4:41pm  Jun 11, 2010 4:41pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar141371_2.gif) kraven](kraven)

  * Joined Apr 2010 | Status: happy as a pig in shit. | [1,448 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=141371)

Yes terminex it's the 1hr  
  
Niceguy can you post the "multi-chart" indi please.  
  
I'm going to throw something in from another thread from FF as I'm having a fair bit of success mixing the two threads together. Same principle as here,   
  
Any pair?? (i use G/U mainly)  
1hr chart  
  
5mins or so before the bar closes just take a look, get the feel of is the bar going more up or down.   
  
At the close of the bar check the bull/bear helper (green up/white down).   
  
if it's green and the **last chart bar was up** (important!!) then wait for new bar to move up 5pips and buy. If you've been watching the bar 5mins before and you see it moving up it often leads to a better trade and fills you with more confidence of a quick entry.  
  
If the bull/bear helper is green and the last bar was red. No trade  
  
For a sell. If the last bar was down and the bullbear is white, wait for new bar to move 5pips down and enter.  
  
you can get more info on the bull bear strength by going into indi's opening the bull indi, open the bear indi (standard on metatrader)then opening the data window. This will give you a precise bulls to bears number. Hope this is clear as it works well when you get the hang of it.  
  
SL 15  
TG that's up to you, i go for 15 but if the price keeps going up i'll stay in. If the price has moved up a lot through the day I'll not stop long.  
  
hope this makes sense

  * Jun 11, 2010 5:18pm  Jun 11, 2010 5:18pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar141371_2.gif) kraven](kraven)

  * Joined Apr 2010 | Status: happy as a pig in shit. | [1,448 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=141371)

Ok  
  
The chart realy isn't much good as you will see a green bar followed by a red- but you need to see how high this bar went bfore it turned back as that's your profit.  
  
You'll see the bull bear help is green all the way  
  
the bars with the tick are our first signal bar. If these a green (up) and the bull bear is Green (up) we buy the next bar (one's with the arrow) wait for it to go up 5pips (ish) before buying. that's it.

  * [#365](/thread/post/3811352#post3811352 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 18, 2010 12:44pm  Jun 18, 2010 12:44pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar5678_4.gif) Pip Rage](pip*rage)

  * | Joined Jan 2006  | Status: Trader | [73 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=5678)

This works on any TF but I found it results on a 1 hr TF became truly exceptional when I applied S/R and candlesticks as filters.  
It rarely fails when the turnaround candle forms an engulfing pattern or is a longwicked reversal candle.  
I also would rather see it break thru strong resistance or support.  
  
In other words, it’s a great method but it needs to be tempered by common sense.

  * Jul 10, 2010 11:34pm  Jul 10, 2010 11:34pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar125201_2.gif) tradestar1](tradestar1)

  * Joined Nov 2009 | Status: Trader | [996 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=125201)

read the rules again....... pick the best time of day....... use rational leverage....... and FORWARD TEST on a demo account.  
Back testers are such BS.  
Was your back tester running a 24 hr period or was it testing only during the peak trading periods?...6 GMT - 15 GMT you know... when london starts and overlaps into N.Y. for about 3 hours.  
What was your SL...... did you actually have one or did you just let it run to close of the candle?  
  
Basically what I saw on your equity curve was extremely unlikely.  
  
So at the risk of being redundant .... I shall reiterate......... Forward test on a demo account and toss the toy back tester.

> Disliked
> 
> Howdy Folks,  
>    
>  Just wanted to share a high probability trading system to you. Its very simple, just pull out a 1hour chart any currency.  
>    
>  Now simply wait for a bull or bear candle to form, after it closes bullish or bearish, ITS MOST LIKELY the next candle will form bull or bear candle...theres some easy pips for you.  
>    
>  Examples:   
>    
>  Bull candle at 8gmt, most likely 9gmt candle could be a bull candle too.  
>  Bear candle at 11gmt, most likely 12gmt candle could be a bear too.  
>    
>  Entry Exit Rules:  
>  Bull candle --- Stoploss at the low of the previous candle,...
> 
> Ignored

RD:  
  
The only candles I use for this method are ones with no wicks to the closing side. When the hour is almost over, I also watch the M1 timeframe to monitor the price action closely. I also don't trade against the trend...much safer. And don't trade this method around news times.  
  
I trade USD/JPN only due to its low volatility.  
  
I have had pretty good success with the few trades I did. 3 wins, no losses, but I go for small pips, usually around 5 so the trade is not open for long periods.  
  
  
-Jacob

  * Aug 5, 2010 12:20am  Aug 5, 2010 12:20am 

  * [ losingtrades](losingtrades)

  * | Joined Jun 2010  | Status: Trader | [246 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=145210)

> [Quoting RED-Dragon](/thread/post/3922043#post3922043 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Thanks Jacob  
>    
>  I don't have the time to be behind the screen much but it is nice to add methods to one's library.  
>  I normally trade Pa on the daily TF so I would battle dropping to 1 min to watch for PA.  
>  I will take trades in the direction of the daily trend.

>  Frank
> 
> Ignored

  
  
Frank...one good thing about this system is that it only requires me to begin looking at the charts about 5 minutes before each hour is up. If the H1 candle is not a good one (big wicks, no clear direction), I wait for the next hour.  
  
If the candle has potential, during those five minutes, I watch the PA on the M1 chart. Then, when the H1 is over, I watch the PA on the M1 chart and see which direction the market goes during the first 20 seconds or so to see if the momentum carried over from the last hour.  
  
All in all, it isn't much time to review the charts for me.  
  
  
-Jacob

  * [ chiba_san](chiba_san)

  * | Joined Jul 2010  | Status: Trader | [420 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=148645)

well, personally, i think this will work. but not for the mentioned 10->20 pips. that's rubbish.   
  
you would need to wait for the close of the candle.   
  
i cannot say how many times you will win in say 100 tries. but the most important thing i can see is this:   
  
1) trade only during market movement  
2) you don't need to even win 50% of the time. even winning 40% of the time or less should yield positive results since your wins will certainly be larger than your losses. it is feasible that you may get whipped a couple times in a row, then one win will get it all back.  
  
i do have one question though. my question is, what is your psychology with one candle?? are you saying that if the price has been moving upwards in the last 60 minutes, that it is more likely for it to move up in the NEXT 60 minutes, but not the next 100 minutes? or next 120 minutes for example? what is your reasoning behind this? would it not be better to define an X amount of time that you feel it should keep moving up and then just close at that time based on say your computers clock?

Yupp. trade with the trend... That's it.  
Look for support and resistance watch out for market times...  
London open, NY open, news releases, London close, etc.

pivot points...  
"When this, then that, if this, then that"... trading systems don't work in the long run...  
They just don't work... As convenient as it would be if they would work, they don't work...

  * [#415](/thread/post/4608810#post4608810 "Post Permalink")

  * May 11, 2011 2:26pm  May 11, 2011 2:26pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar69360_3.gif) primzvicious](primzvicious)

  * | Joined May 2008  | Status: Ad Astra Per Aspera | [1,741 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=69360)

well i sometimes used candle formation as an entry and target... however your system needs some filtering in determining true or false signal...  
  
to determine true/false signal i added a **new rule** as follow:  
  
\- bearish/ bullish signal should started from fresh top or fresh bottom which follow by the same next candle (bear-bear or bull/bull)  
\- the minimum target is breaking the top of the second candle (if it was bull) or breaking the low of the second candle (if it was bear)  
\- the stop should be above or below the fresh top  
heres i filter your signal... it may help ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)  
  
regards..

> [Quoting primzvicious](/thread/post/4608810#post4608810 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> well i sometimes used candle formation as an entry and target... however your system needs some filtering in determining true or false signal...  
>    
>  to determine true/false signal i added a **new rule** as follow:  
>    
>  \- bearish/ bullish signal should started from fresh top or fresh bottom which follow by the same next candle (bear-bear or bull/bull)  
>  \- the minimum target is breaking the top of the second candle (if it was bull) or breaking the low of the second candle (if it was bear)  
>  \- the stop should be above or below the fresh top  
>  heres i...
> 
> Ignored

heres an example... hope it works ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)

in my practice the best trend`s indicator is CCI_50 (Supertrend). you also may use EMA_5 + EMA_8.   
within the confines of Tonys system they work well  
all the best signals after pullbacks to the indicators lines.   
mean, the very first trend_color candle after pullback is a "signal candle". so may use stop orders to trade it

  * Oct 27, 2011 3:25am  Oct 27, 2011 3:25am 

  * [ Roofx](roofx)

  * | Joined Jul 2010  | Status: Trader | [406 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=149701)

Sorry to be a party pooper here guys but realistically the system will not work on the long term. 10-20 pip TP is too little when placing the stop on the other size of the previous candle as this is usually more than 10-20 pips.   
  
I might be stating the obvious but if a system so basic could really generate consistent gains and grow an account indefinately, don't you think the banks and big traders would just use a simple EA to follow this very system and everyone would be stinking rich?  
  
I'll get shot down for this no doubt but listen to me guys. Stop looking for an automatic follow the green light system. You need to actually use your brains to make pips in this business. Every trade is different and the market state is relevent to how you should go about it.   
  
The system forum is 99% nonsense and 1% actual credible trading advice. But sadly the profitable traders need the forex world to be filled with garbage systems to fool the newbies and hopefuls into risking their capital on some basic mechanical system that looks good on back test, to provide liquidity for the people who acually know how the market works.  
  
I have been there and done it all too, following amazing looking systems, making my own (dozens of them) and I was never profitable for more than a month or two until I realised it was time to delete all the garbage from my charts and follow price action. The M1 Stochastic is useful for getting a more precise entry when it's time to take a trade but most of everything else is just nonsense guys. Seriously. Give yourselves a fighting chance and stop looking for the holy grail or a magical system that will make money for you. Use the common sense to realise it does not exist. It can't exist. If it was that easy everyone would be doing it and the markets would cease to function.

Well. This is one example.  
  
I saw 2 Bullish candle on Euro/USD chart. So, I placed a pending "buy stop" order (22101904) at the high of the second bullish candle.(1.4002) and Stop loss at previous candle's low, which is 1.3965. My target profit Only 10 pips because previous post mentioned that you will have 90% chance to hit your target. See Chart 1 for my trade setup.  
  
I waited for almost 1 hour and check back my trade. Bingo! my trade was done and I made 10 pips profit. See Chart 2 for my trade history. The trade was trigger arround 2011.10.27 06:51 and done at 2011.10.27 06:53.  
  
I tried the system last time on demo account but this time is my real account. My lot size was small (0.01) because I got insufficient fund in my account. I will try it out again some more times to gain more confidient before I increase my lot size.  
  
Anyway. Thank you. Tony.

  * [#440](/thread/post/6513175#post6513175 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 14, 2013 7:40am  Mar 14, 2013 7:40am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar261607_1.gif) tinny79](tinny79)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Jun 2012 | [73 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=261607)

This style is basically the same as what i use except I use on daily chart and success ratio is at 80% or a little higher, however i use opposing candle to get out and breakeven at 40 pips.. Often get 150 to 300 pip trades and so thought i would share..  
  
You cannot use robots or ea's with this technique, because with this technique you need common sense as well and a robot does not have it.. The two candle entry technique to work well one has to see candle movement down first for bull entry and move up for bear entry..   
  
The waves of the market.. The market moves in waves, look at the daily, 4 to 5 candles down, up move, 4 to 5 candles up then down move.. Assess the wave even in trending markets there is waves.. Then use the two candle to get in.. Logic is needed..  
  
One cannot just enter randomly on second candle anywhere like an ea.. Plus look at support and resistance for even more success..   
  
My friend there is no such thing as a successful robot, they just cant calculate logic like what Tony says on first or second page.. And by the way tony, thanks for sharing your knowledge, I do not trade the 1 hour but will consider checking it out as well..

  * Mar 28, 2013 7:10am  Mar 28, 2013 7:10am 

  * [ puppypippy](puppypippy)

  * | Joined Feb 2010  | Status: Trader | [252 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=132518)

This system is easy to debunk. It's equivalent to flipping a coin only your odds are worse which is why Tony is no where to be found. If this system worked the guy would be the king of forex. Internationally known as the guy who finally figured out forex and the whole world would be using this system using robots to make millions. But no he is just another person who had a run of luck then cleared out, when his luck started going against him. That actually is what most of the traders on this forum do, while telling you they have been trading this system for years and doing it full time.  
  
You can debunk this yourself in minutes. Simply go back a few hundred bars and start counting. Count one when two bars occur and then minus one when they don't You will be shocked at how often 2 bars DON'T occur. In fact it may be better to bet on them not occurring!  
  
Calling it price action is just silly. All price movement is price action! Saying that you have cracked the code to how price moves then never being heard from again is ridiculous.  
  
Adding different time frames, other criteria like waiting for 5 pips to be reached, is all just smoke and mirrors to hide the fact this system stinks LOL  
  
Do you home work before losing money on this silly system. Count how often two of the same bar occurs. Instead of thinking like a gambler and having confidence after a run of winners because there is a bigger run of losers coming just around the corner with this system.

Sure, they're successful in developing sophisticated machines (and gadgets), but they should get away from this idea that life is totally 'mechanical' and 'random' (evolution theory, explaining complex systems being the outcome of random events is just too silly for words). Just my two cents, as they say :-)

Back-test for EURJPY, 1H, 2015:  
40% win ratio, account balance -55%

47% win ratio, account balance -47%

Any "system" which causes trader to take 10 pips profit while SL size is 0.00000000000000000001% larger than profit is not worth testing. Otherwise you would need more than 80% trade success rate over a very long period...In his best days it is said Jessie Livermoore had 79%, but that's just a rumor...  
Once I had (3 years ago) 36 consecutive trades with profit over a 3 month period. In the next 20 days I burned my account. Target profit NEEDS to be larger than stoploss size...otherwise your'e a sitting duck and the number of hunters with rifles around you grows exponentialy with each successful trade ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)

> {quote} Hey, have a look at the image. In that you can see a color coded system that shows the price action on a minute-by-minute basis, so you can know how good the trade is currently. You can also see the hourly candle inside the 1minute chart and i have installed an indicator where you can see horizontal levels 20pips away from each other which you can use for ideal take profit levels n stuff. I like simple systems like this one (thanks Tony!). Not so sure if more information equals more money though... More information takes the simplicity away from any simple system and opens the door for disturbing emotions (doubt/fear/greed...). Why not simply keep simple systems simple? :-)  
  
Keep your losses small (first of all, do no harm ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60e.png?v=15.1)) and move on to the next trade when price goes about 8-10 pips against you seems like a good rule of thumb here.   
  
Cheers! 

95% of the people don't believe 100% they can win, that's why they lose

  * [#466](/thread/post/12987778#post12987778 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 9:11pm  Jun 7, 2020 3:15am | Edited 9:11pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar568387_1.gif) de5151](de5151)

  * Joined Mar 2017 | Status: Trader | [159 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=568387)

This system would be very effective by including the Choppiness Index indicator (attached below) to your chart to know that you are not in a ranging time.  
  
Go to youtube and search "Secret Swing Trading Indicator To Avoid Ranges (Choppiness Index Strategies)" by The Secret Mindset to see how this thing works (I have no association).  
  
I like simple systems like Tony's Two Candles and this would improve the odds. 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [choppiness index.mq4](/attachment/file/3657171?d=1591467331) 4 KB | 377 downloads 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [2 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#467](/thread/post/12988258#post12988258 "Post Permalink")

  * Jun 7, 2020 10:07pm  Jun 7, 2020 10:07pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar568387_1.gif) de5151](de5151)

  * Joined Mar 2017 | Status: Trader | [159 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=568387)

He also mentions using volume with choppiness. I use the better volume indicator (attached below) because I can put it right into the Choppiness Index window.  
  
Better Volume colors are the following:  
Blue -- normal volume  
Yellow -- low volume  
Green -- large volume by hedge funds opening or closing -- maybe a change in direction coming (I change this color to white)  
Red -- large amount of buyers over sellers -- will most likely change to bullish (I change this color to lime-- to me green means up)  
White -- large amount of sellers over buyers -- will most likely change to bearish (I change this color to red -- to me red means down)  
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: better-volume-2.png
Size: 11 KB](/attachment/image/3657395/thumbnail?d=1591535380)](/attachment/image/3657395?d=1591535380)

![File Type: ex4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/ex4.gif) [BetterVolume.ex4](/attachment/file/3657393?d=1591535264) 38 KB | 306 downloads
